                  <form>       
                     <itype>1</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">تَرَكَهُ</orth>

                  </form>, (S, M, Msb, K, &amp;c.,) aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bu" lang="ar">تَرُكَ</orth>
                  </form>, (S, M,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">تَرْكٌ</foreign> (S, M, Msb, K, &amp;c.) and <foreign lang="ar">ترْكَانٌ</foreign>, with kesr, (Fr, K,) <hi rend="ital">He left it, forsook it, relinquished it, abandoned it, deserted it,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">quitted it;</hi> either <hi rend="ital">intentionally, and by choice,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">by constraint, and of necessity:</hi> (Er-Rághib, TA:) <hi rend="ital">he left it, forsook it,</hi> &amp;c., as above; namely, a thing that he desired, or wished for, and also a thing that he did not desire, or did not wish for: (Ibn-'Arafeh, TA:) <hi rend="ital">he left it, quitted it, went away from it,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">departed from it;</hi> namely, a place: and <hi rend="ital">he left him, forsook him, relinquished him, abandoned him, deserted him, quitted him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">separated himself from him:</hi> (Msb:) <hi rend="ital">he cast it,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">threw it, away, as a thing of no account; rejected it; discarded it; cast it off; left it off:</hi> (MF, TA:) <hi rend="ital">he left it, left it alone, let it alone; ceased, desisted, forbore,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">abstained, from it; neglected it, omitted it,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">left it undone;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">خَلَّاهُ</foreign>; (S, A, O;) or <foreign lang="ar">وَدَعَهُ</foreign>; (M, K;) as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n3904-1" target="اتّركهُ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>. (K. [But respecting this latter verb, see what follows.]) <foreign lang="ar">وَٱتْرُكِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">البَحْرَ رَهْوًا</foreign>, in the Kur xliv. 23, <hi rend="ital">And leave thou the sea opened with a wide interval;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">motionless,</hi> in the same state as before thy passing through it, and strike it not with thy rod, nor alter anything thereof; (Bd;) or <hi rend="ital">motionless, parted asunder;</hi> (Jel;) so that the Egyptians may enter it; (Bd, Jel;) is an instance of the verb meaning leaving intentionally, and by choice: (Er-Rághib, TA:) and <foreign lang="ar">كَمْ تَرَكُوا مِنْ جَنَّاتٍ وَعُيُونٍ</foreign>, in the next verse, <hi rend="ital">How many gardens and springs did they leave!</hi> (Jel,) is an instance of the verb meaning leaving by constraint, and of necessity. (Er-Rághib, TA.) In a phrase such as <foreign lang="ar">تَرَكَ حَقَّهُ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">He made his right,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">due,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">claim, to be null,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">he rejected it,</hi> and such as <foreign lang="ar">تَرَكَ رَكْعَةٌ مِنَ الصَّلَاةِ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">He neglected, omitted,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">left unperformed, a</hi> 
                  <pb n="305"/> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ركعة</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">of the prayer,</hi> [it is said (but I think it doubtful) that] the verb, having an ideal substantive for its objective complement, is used metaphorically. (Msb.)   
      <foreign lang="ar">قَالَ فِيهِ فَمَا <ref cref="n3904-2" target="ٱتَّرَكَ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> means <foreign lang="ar">مَا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">تَرَكَ شَيْئًا</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">He strove, laboured,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">exerted himself,</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">اِجْتَهَدَ</foreign>,) <hi rend="ital">in it, and neglected not,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">omitted not, anything</hi> in his power]: the verb is of the measure <foreign lang="ar">اِفْتَعَلَ</foreign>. (S.) <foreign lang="ar">مَنْ أَوْصَى بِالثُّلُثِ وَلَمْ  <ref cref="n3904-3" target="يَتَّرِكْ" n="3" type="6" subtype="FTFSO" lang="ar"/> شَيْئًا</foreign> is a mistake for <foreign lang="ar">ولم يَتْرُكْ شَيْئًا</foreign>, or <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n3904-4" target="يَتَّرِكْ" n="4" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>ولم</foreign> without <foreign lang="ar">شَيْئًا</foreign>, or <foreign lang="ar">فَمَا ٱتَّرَكَ</foreign>; for this verb is not trans., except, sometimes, in poetry; and the meaning is, <foreign lang="ar">وَلَمْ يَتْرُكْ فِيمَاأُذِنَ لَهُ فِيهِ شَيْئًا</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">He who bequeaths the third</hi> of his property, <hi rend="ital">and does not omit anything</hi> of what he is allowed (to leave, or anything of the third part, for this is all that he is allowed to bequeath)]: it is from the saying   
      <foreign lang="ar">فَعَلَ فَمَا <ref cref="n3904-5" target="ٱتَّرَكَ" n="5" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He did</hi> such a thing, <hi rend="ital">and neglected not,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">omitted not, anything</hi>]. (Mgh.) You say also, <foreign lang="ar">تَرَكَ المَيِّتُ مَالًا</foreign>, i. e. <hi rend="ital">The deceased left property.</hi> (Msb.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">وَتَرَكْنَا عَلَيْهِ فِى الآخِرِينَ</foreign>, (K,) in the Kur [xxxvii. 76 &amp;c.], (TA,) means <hi rend="ital">And we have perpetuated</hi> (K, Jel, TA) <hi rend="ital">to him</hi> a eulogy <hi rend="ital">among the later generations</hi> (Jel, TA) of the prophets and peoples to the day of resurrection, [namely,] Salutation &amp;c. (Jel.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">التَّرْكُ</foreign> is also <hi rend="ital">syn. with</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الجَعْلُ</foreign>, (Lth, K, TA,) in some instances; (Lth, TA;) as though it had two contr. significations: (K:) [i. e.,] when <foreign lang="ar">تَرَكَ</foreign> is doubly trans., it has the meaning of <foreign lang="ar">صَيَّرَ</foreign>, (MF, TA,) or <foreign lang="ar">جَعَلَ</foreign>. (TA.) So in the saying, <foreign lang="ar">تَرَكْتُ الحَبْلَ شَدِيدًا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">I made,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">rendered, the rope strong;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">made it,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">caused it, to be,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">become, strong.</hi> (TA.) So too in the Kur ii. 16, <foreign lang="ar">وَتَرَكَهُمْ فِى ظُلُمَاتٍ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">And maketh,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">causeth, them to be in darknesses.</hi> (Ksh, Bd, MF.) And sometimes one says of any action that has come at last to a certain state, <foreign lang="ar">مَا تَرَكْتُهُ كَذَا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I did not make it,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">cause it, to be thus</hi>]. (TA.)       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">تَرِكَ</foreign>, aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Ba" lang="ar">تَرَكَ</orth>
                  </form>, (IAar, K,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">تَرْكٌ</foreign>, (TK,) <hi rend="ital">He</hi> (a man, IAar) <hi rend="ital">married,</hi> i. e. <hi rend="ital">took to wife, a</hi>

                  </form> [inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">مُتَارَكَةٌ</foreign>] is <hi rend="ital">syn. with</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">خَالَاهُ</foreign> (S in art. <foreign lang="ar">خلو</foreign>) [which is explained in the K, in art. <foreign lang="ar">خلو</foreign>, as <hi rend="ital">syn. with</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">تَرَكَهُ</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">He left, forsook, relinquished, abandoned,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">him</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it;</hi> and thus it may often be well rendered: but it properly signifies <hi rend="ital">he left him, forsook him,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">being left,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">by him;</hi> whence it is said in the Mgh, in art. <foreign lang="ar">ودع</foreign>, that <foreign lang="ar">مُوَادَعَةُ</foreign> is syn. with <foreign lang="ar">مُصَالَحَةٌ</foreign> because it is <foreign lang="ar">مُتَارَكَةٌ</foreign>: Golius, as on the authority of Ibn-Maaroof, explains <foreign lang="ar">تاركهُ</foreign> as signifying <hi rend="ital">he dismissed him, and did not molest him: he left him unmolested</hi> is one of its meanings, but is not the primary signification: accord. to the TK, <foreign lang="ar">متاركة</foreign> signifies the <hi rend="ital">leaving,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">anything in the state in which it is:</hi> and the <hi rend="ital">leaving,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">one another</hi>]. One says also, <foreign lang="ar">تَارَكْتُهُ البَيْعَ</foreign>, (S, Mgh, but in the latter <foreign lang="ar">تَارَكَهُ</foreign>, and in the TA <foreign lang="ar">فِى البَيْعِ</foreign>,) <foreign lang="ar">وَغَيْرَهُ</foreign>, (Mgh,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">مُتَارَكَةٌ</foreign>, (S,) [app. meaning <hi rend="ital">I relinquished with him,</hi> i. e. <hi rend="ital">concurrently with him, the sale, &amp;c.:</hi> see 6, by which this rendering is confirmed: Golius, as on the authority of J, who has not explained it, says that it means <hi rend="ital">I relinquished to him the merchandise,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">commodity;</hi> and Freytag follows him.]          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  [Hence,] <foreign lang="ar">مُتَارَكَةٌ</foreign> is metonymically used as meaning The <hi rend="ital">making peace</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">a truce</hi>], or <hi rend="ital">reconciling oneself, with another</hi> or <hi rend="ital">others.</hi> (Mgh.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  In the saying, <foreign lang="ar">لَا بَارَكَ ٱللّٰهُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">فِيِهِ وَلَا تَارَكَ وَلَا دَارَكَ</foreign>, it is an imitative sequent, (K,) all of these verbs having the same meaning [so that the saying may be rendered <hi rend="ital">May God not bless him nor felicitate him nor make him happy</hi>]: (TA:) [or the meaning may be, <hi rend="ital">nor preserve him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">prolong his life;</hi> for] IAar says that <foreign lang="ar">تَارَكَ</foreign> means <foreign lang="ar">أَبْقَى</foreign>. <orth extent=\"full\" lang=\"ar\">تراك</orth>\n                  </form> an imperative verbal noun, meaning <foreign lang=\"ar\">اُتْرُكْ</foreign> [<hi rend=\"ital\">Leave thou,</hi> &amp;c.]. (S, TA.) Hence the saying, <foreign lang=\"ar\">تَرَاكِ تَرَاكِ صُحْبَةَ الأَتْرَاكِ</foreign> [<hi rend=\"ital\">Leave thou, leave thou, the companionship of the Turks</hi>]. (TA.) Yoo says that <foreign lang=\"ar\">تَرَاكَ</foreign> is a dial. var. of the same; but this is only when it is used as a prefixed noun, as in <foreign lang=\"ar\">تَرَاكَهَا</foreign> for <foreign lang=\"ar\">تَرَاكِهَا</foreign>.
